--- Step-01: Introduction to Docker BuildKit ---

Welcome back.
In this demo we are going to learn about Docker build kit in detail.
So let's understand the Docker build architecture on a high level.
So here in Docker build architecture we are going to have client and server.
Client is nothing but our command which we are going to run.
So we are going to run docker build exe as the command.
And that is the command we will use to create the Docker images.
And that command will be sent to the build kit server, the back end builder that actually executes
the build processes.
And these build kit servers will have local builders and also remote builders.
So local builders are nothing but which are present on our local desktop.
And remote builders are which are present on the Docker build cloud.
Now if you see here, this build kit is nothing, but it is an advanced build engine that replaces the
legacy Docker builder and it is available from Docker Engine version 2323 version as the default builder,
and it provides enhanced performance like build speed, efficiency and also lot of new features.
It also allows us to run multiple builds at a time with optimized caching.
So which means it provides means like using this build kit, you can create or run parallel builds,
and also it has a efficient cache management.
And in addition to that it has reduced build times, which leads to increased productivity.
And also it have the effective secret management and enhanced security.
And it allows us to connect the remote builders in our local desktop so that our build will run on the
remote builders, which are present on the Docker build cloud.
And we can also create multi-platform Docker images.
So this build kit supports multi-platform For building multi-platform Docker images.
So let us see what exactly that means.
So if you go to Hub.docker.com and if you type any of the Docker image.
So let's say like nginx right.
And if you go to the nginx docker image and if you go to the tags here and take any of the tag right.
So any of the tag, if you take it in this tag, you see this is a single tag, but you have multiple
Docker images created as part of OS and architecture operating system architecture.
So one Docker image for Linux 386.
So this is built using means like this is built using Linux 386.
And it supports only on Linux 386 in the same way this is built for Linux Amd64.
This is this one is built for Linux Armv5 this for Armv7.
And this is for ARM 64 V8.
So like this we can build a Docker image which supports multiple operating system architectures.
So that is possible using this build kit, and it generates multi-platform supported Docker images at
a time, so you can run a single Docker build command and provide multiple platforms there.
And it creates a Docker image with multiple platforms in it with a single command itself.
So you don't need to run multiple times a single command.
Support for this environment.
With a single environment you can create all these, uh, supported Docker, all the operating system
architectures, whatever you want to create the Docker images.
Or you can create with a single command.
And in the next demo we are going to see that in detail right now.
Another important thing which we need to know is builders.

the builders, we will find the builders here.

--- Step-01: Introduction to Docker Build Cloud ---

Welcome back.
In this demo we are going to learn about Docker Build Cloud.
So what is Docker Build Cloud.
It is a cloud based build service for Docker images which provides scalable remote infrastructure to
handle builds, especially for resource intensive or multi-platform projects, so primarily used for
resource intensive or multi-platform projects.
So its infrastructure is highly scalable.
When we compare it with our local desktop, local desktop, we have a limited infrastructure, but here
in the cloud it can be scaled to unlimited infrastructure.
Due to that, the amount of time it takes to complete a build is going to be very short means like we
can speed up our build process and it also allows for concurrent operations on large projects.
So there are multiple advantages to using Docker build cloud.
And it also supports the multi-platform building multi-platform Docker images using single process.
It is same as build kit whatever is available in local.
It is also the same available on the cloud.
Only thing is we see a high performance here.
And in addition to that, effective cash management and also we see improved security and secrets management.
Right.
So all the sensitive data is safely stored in the cloud, ensures only during the build process and
never included in the final image.
So that's about security and secret management and for build caching also it reuses cached layers from
previous builds stored in the cloud, reducing build times and resource usage, especially for frequently
updated applications.
Right.
So that's the key important thing.
These are the benefits about Docker build cloud.
Let's go ahead and then practically implement it.
And in our demo what we are going to do is we are going to create one Docker image using Docker Build
Cloud and the other Docker image using local builder and see the performance how much each one takes,
so that it will be easy for us to know that how build cloud is highly performant, then a local desktop
builders.
And another important thing here to note is build cloud is not free for a basic free plan user.
You cannot implement this demo, so this is a optional demo for you.

--- Step-01: Introduction to Docker Multi-stage Builds ---

Welcome back.
In this demo we are going to learn about Docker multi-stage builds.
So these multi-stage Docker file keeps the final image lightweight by avoiding build tools and development
dependencies in the final stage.
So if you see here right in the stage one, in the builder stage, you are saying from node bookworm
as builder, right?
And we are using the Workdir slash app.
And this is a simple uh, node NodeJS application.
So we are going to copy package.json file also to app directory and install the Node.js related uh packages
and which are also at production level only.
Now ideally we can we don't need to use production flag, but still we are ensuring that we need only
production grade packages here.
So we have used the flag hyphen hyphen production.
And we are also going to copy the uh, JS files present in our directory to this respective, stage
one.
And after that, what we are going to do is we will start the stage two right in the stage two.
What we are going to do is we are going to use node Bookworm Slim here.
We have used the uh, major image.
And then here we have used still the slimmer image as final uh stage.
And we have used the Workdir slash app and copy from builder stage hyphen hyphen from equal to builder,
which means from this builder stage in slash app directory.
What is there in the builder stage?
Copy to this directory.
Dot slash means dot current directory, which is again here.
Also it is to slash app directory only expose port 8080 and then start the Node.js application.
So this is what we have done on a high level.
But what happens here is we are going to make our final Docker image very lightweight.
We will avoid any build tools or development dependencies which can be included in stage one, and which
do not need to be included in the final stage.
Only production dependencies and necessary application code are included in the final stage, which
reduces the image size and also the potential attack surface from the security perspective, and you
can see that the final image will be very lightweight when compared to the, uh, single stage build
when you run it.
Okay, so as we are using the node Bookworm Slim in the final stage further reduces the image size compared
to the full node bookworm image making deployments faster and also resource efficient.
And also we will have the improved security by using these multi-stage Docker builds by keeping only
production dependencies and excluding all unnecessary build files.
This approach reduces the risk of vulnerabilities the smaller the image size also makes it easier to
audit and also manage.
